                                                  THE EXISTENCE OF DESIGNS VIA ITERATIVE ABSORPTION:
                                                        HYPERGRAPH F -DESIGNS FOR ARBITRARY F

                                                             STEFAN GLOCK, DANIELA KUМҲHN, ALLAN LO AND DERYK OSTHUS


                                                   Abstract. We solve the existence problem for F -designs for arbitrary r-uniform hypergraphs F .
                                                   This implies that given any r-uniform hypergraph F , the trivially necessary divisibility conditions
                                                   are suп¬ғcient to guarantee a decomposition of any suп¬ғciently large complete r-uniform hypergraph
                                                   into edge-disjoint copies of F , which answers a question asked e.g. by Keevash. The graph case
                                                   r = 2 was proved by Wilson in 1975 and forms one of the cornerstones of design theory. The
arXiv:1611.06827v3 [math.CO] 28 Feb 2020




                                                   case when F is complete corresponds to the existence of block designs, a problem going back to
                                                   the 19th century, which was recently settled by Keevash. In particular, our argument provides a
                                                   new proof of the existence of block designs, based on iterative absorption (which employs purely
                                                   probabilistic and combinatorial methods).
                                                      Our main result concerns decompositions of hypergraphs whose clique distribution fulп¬Ғlls
                                                   certain regularity constraints. Our argument allows us to employ a вҖҳregularity boostingвҖҷ process
                                                   which frequently enables us to satisfy these constraints even if the clique distribution of the
                                                   original hypergraph does not satisfy them. This enables us to go signiп¬Ғcantly beyond the setting
                                                   of quasirandom hypergraphs considered by Keevash. In particular, we obtain a resilience version
                                                   and a decomposition result for hypergraphs of large minimum degree.




                                                                                         1. Introduction
                                              The term вҖҳcombinatorial designвҖҷ usually refers to a system of finite sets which satisfies some
                                           specified balance or symmetry condition. Some well known examples include balanced incomplete
                                           block designs, projective planes, Latin squares and Hadamard matrices. These have applications
                                           in many areas such as finite geometry, statistics, experiment design and cryptography.
                                           1.1. Background. In this paper,1 we consider block designs and more generally F -designs, which
                                           can be conveniently defined using graph theoretical terminology. A hypergraph G is a pair (V, E),
                                           where V = V (G) is the vertex set of G and the edge set E is a set of subsets of V . We often
                                           identify G with E, in particular, we let |G| := |E|. We say that G is an r-graph if every edge has
                                                                (r)
                                           size r. We let Kn denote the complete r-graph on n vertices.
                                              Let G and F be r-graphs. An F -decomposition of G is a collection F of copies of F in G
                                           such that every edge of G is contained in exactly one of these copies. (Throughout the paper,
                                           we always assume that F is non-empty without mentioning this explicitly.) More generally, an
                                           (F, О»)-design of G is a collection F of distinct copies of F in G such that every edge of G is
                                           contained in exactly О» of these copies. As discussed in Section 1.2, such a design can only exist
                                           if G satisfies certain divisibility conditions (e.g. if F is a graph triangle and О» = 1, then G must
                                           have even vertex degrees and the number of edges must be a multiple of three). If F and G are
                                           complete, such designs are also referred to as block designs. More precisely, an (n, f, r, О»)-block
                                           design (or r-(n, f, О»)-block design) is a set X of f -subsets of some n-set V , such that every r-
                                           subset of V belongs to exactly О» elements of X. The f -subsets are often called вҖҳblocksвҖҷ. An
                                           (n, f, r, 1)-block design is also called an (n, f, r)-Steiner system. Note that an (n, f, r, О»)-block
                                                            (r)                (r)
                                           design is a (Kf , О»)-design of Kn .
                                              The question of the existence of such designs goes back to the 19th century. For instance,
                                           Steiner asked in 1853 for which parameters Steiner systems exist. The first general result was due
                                              Date: 2nd March 2020.
                                              The research leading to these results was partially supported by the EPSRC, grant nos. EP/N019504/1
                                           (D. KuМҲhn) and EP/P002420/1 (A. Lo), by the Royal Society and the Wolfson Foundation (D. KuМҲhn) as well as
                                           by the European Research Council under the European UnionвҖҷs Seventh Framework Programme (FP/2007вҖ“2013)
                                           / ERC Grant Agreement no. 306349 (S. Glock and D. Osthus).
                                              1This paper combines the two manuscripts arXiv:1611.06827v1 and arXiv:1706.01800.


                                                                                                    1
2                              S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



to Kirkman [26], who proved the existence of Steiner triple systems (i.e. triangle decompositions
of complete graphs) under the appropriate divisibility conditions. In fact, the existence conjecture
postulated that for any given parameters f, r, О», the necessary divisibility conditions are sufficient
for the existence of an (n, f, r, О»)-block design for all sufficiently large n. In a ground-breaking
series of papers which transformed the area, Wilson [47, 48, 49, 50] solved the existence problem
in the graph setting (i.e. when r = 2) by showing that for any graph F the trivially necessary
                                                                     (2)
divisibility conditions imply the existence of (F, О»)-designs in Kn for sufficiently large n.
   For r вүҘ 3, much less was known until very recently. Answering a question of ErdoМӢs and
Hanani [16], RoМҲdl [40] was able to give an approximate solution to the existence conjecture by
                                                                       (r)     (r)
constructing near optimal packings of edge-disjoint copies of Kf in Kn , i.e. constructing a
                                          (r)                                             (r)
collection of edge-disjoint copies of Kf which cover almost all the edges of Kn . (For this,
he introduced his now famous RoМҲdl nibble method, which has since had a major impact in
many areas.) His bounds were subsequently improved by increasingly sophisticated randomised
techniques (see e.g. [1, 46]). Ferber, Hod, Krivelevich and Sudakov [17] recently observed that
this method can be used to obtain an вҖҳalmostвҖҷ Steiner system in the sense that every r-set is
covered by either one or two f -sets.
   Teirlinck [45] was the first to prove the existence of infinitely many non-trivial (n, f, r, О»)-block
designs for arbitrary r вүҘ 6, via an ingenious recursive construction based on the symmetric group
(this however requires f = r + 1 and О» large compared to f ). Kuperberg, Lovett and Peled [31]
proved a вҖҳlocalized central limit theoremвҖҷ for rigid combinatorial structures, which implies the
existence of designs for arbitrary f and r, but again for large О». There are many constructions
resulting in sporadic and infinite families of designs (see e.g. the handbook [13]). However, the
set of parameters they cover is very restricted. In particular, even the existence of infinitely many
Steiner systems with r вүҘ 4 was open until recently.
   In a recent breakthrough, Keevash [23] proved the existence of (n, f, r, О»)-block designs for
arbitrary (but fixed) r, f and О», provided n is sufficiently large and satisfies the trivially necessary
divisibility conditions. In particular, his result implies the existence of Steiner systems for any
admissible range of parameters as long as n is sufficiently large compared to f . The approach
in [23] involved randomised algebraic constructions and yielded a far-reaching generalisation to
block designs in quasirandom r-graphs.
   Here we develop a non-algebraic approach based on iterative absorption, which additionally
yields resilience versions and the existence of block designs in hypergraphs of large minimum
degree. Moreover, we are able to go beyond the setting of block designs and show that F -designs
also exist for arbitrary r-graphs F whenever the necessary divisibility conditions are satisfied.




1.2. F -designs in quasirandom hypergraphs. We now describe the degree conditions which
are trivially necessary for the existence of an F -design in an r-graph G. For a set S вҠҶ V (G) with
0 вүӨ |S| вүӨ r, the (r вҲ’ |S|)-graph G(S) has vertex set V (G) \ S and contains all (r вҲ’ |S|)-subsets
of V (G) \ S that together with S form an edge in G. (G(S) is often called the link graph of
S.) Let Оҙ(G) and вҲҶ(G) denote the minimum and maximum (r вҲ’ 1)-degree of an r-graph G,
respectively, that is, the minimum/maximum value of |G(S)| over all S вҠҶ V (G) of size r вҲ’ 1. For
a (non-empty) r-graph F , we define the divisibility vector of F as Deg(F ) := (d0 , . . . , drвҲ’1 ) вҲҲ Nr ,
where di := gcd{|F (S)| : S вҲҲ V (F       )

1.3. F -designs in hypergraphs of large minimum degree. Once the existence question
is settled, a next natural step is to seek F -designs and F -decompositions in r-graphs of large
minimum degree. Our next result gives a bound on the minimum degree which ensures an F -
decomposition for вҖҳweakly regularвҖҷ r-graphs F . These are defined as follows.
Definition 1.3 (weakly regular). Let F be an r-graph. We say that F is weakly (s0 , . . . , srвҲ’1 )-
regular if for all 0 вүӨ i вүӨ r вҲ’ 1 and all S вҲҲ V (F       )
                                                         

F is weakly regular if it is weakly (s0 , . . . , srвҲ’1 )-regular for suitable si вҖҷs.
  So for example, cliques, the Fano plane and the octahedron are all weakly regular but a 3-
uniform tight or loose cycle is not.

Definition 1.5 (Decomposition threshold). Given an r-graph F , let ОҙF be the infimum of all
Оҙ вҲҲ [0, 1] with the following property: There exists n0 вҲҲ N such that for all n вүҘ n0 , every

   Previously, the only explicit result for the hypergraph case r вүҘ 3 was due to Yuster [51],
who showed that if T is a linear r-uniform hypertree, then every       T -divisible r-graph G on n
                                                   1            n 
vertices with minimum vertex degree at least ( 2rвҲ’1    + o(1)) rвҲ’1  has a T -decomposition. This is
asymptotically best possible for nontrivial T . Moreover, the result implies that ОҙT вүӨ 1/2rвҲ’1 .
   For the graph case r = 2, much more is known about the decomposition threshold: the results
in [7, 19] establish a close connection between ОҙF and the fractional decomposition threshold
ОҙFвҲ— (which is defined as in Definition 1.5, but with an F -decomposition replaced by a fractional
F -decomposition). In particular, the results in [7, 19] imply that ОҙF вүӨ max{ОҙFвҲ— , 1 вҲ’ 1/(ПҮ(F ) + 1)}
and that ОҙF = ОҙFвҲ— if F is a complete graph.
   Together with recent results on the fractional decomposition threshold for cliques in [6, 14],
this gives the best current bounds on ОҙF for general F . It would be very interesting to establish
a similar connection in the hypergraph case.
   Also, for bipartite graphs the decomposition threshold was completely determined in [19]. It
would be interesting to see if this can be generalised to r-partite r-graphs. On the other hand,
even the decomposition threshold of a graph triangle is still unknown (a beautiful conjecture of
Nash-Williams [36] would imply that the value is 3/4).
1.4. Varying block sizes. We now briefly consider a more general notion of block designs, where
more than just one block order is admissible. Given n, r, О» вҲҲ N as before and A вҠҶ N, we say
that X is an (n, A, r, О»)-block design if X consists of subsets of an n-set V such that |x| вҲҲ A
for every x вҲҲ X and such that every r-subset of V is contained in precisely О» elements of X.
Similarly, given an r-graph G and a family of r-graphs K, we say that F is a K-decomposition of
G if every edge of G lies in precisely one F вҲҲ F and if F вҲҲ K for each F вҲҲ F. For instance, a
    (r)                               (r)
{Ka : a вҲҲ A}-decomposition of Kn is equivalent to an (n, A, r, 1)-block design. We say that
G is K-divisible if gcd{Deg(F )i : F вҲҲ K} | Deg(G)i for all 0 вүӨ i вүӨ r вҲ’ 1. Clearly, K-divisibility
is a necessary condition for the existence of a K-decomposition. Theorem 1.1 easily implies the
following result (see Section 9).
Theorem 1.6 (Designs with varying block sizes). For all f, r вҲҲ N and p вҲҲ (0, 1] there exist c > 0,
h вҲҲ N and n0 вҲҲ N such that the following holds for all n вүҘ n0 . Let K be a family of r-graphs of
                                                                                                 5



order at most f each. Suppose that G is a (c, h, p)-typical r-graph on n vertices. Then G has a
K-decomposition if it is K-divisible.
   As a very special case, Theorem 1.6 resolves a conjecture of Archdeacon on self-dual embeddings
of random graphs in orientable surfaces: as proved in [3], a graph has such an embedding if it
                                                                            (2)
has a {K4 , K5 }-decomposition. (In this paragraph, we write Kn for Kn .) Note that every
graph with an even number of edges is {K4 , K5 }-divisible. Suppose G is a (c, h, p)-typical graph
on n vertices with an even number of edges and 1/n вүӘ c вүӘ 1/h вүӘ p (which almost surely
holds for the binomial random graph Gn,p if we remove at most one edge). Then we can apply
Theorem 1.6 to obtain a {K4 , K5 }-decomposition of G. It was also shown in [3] that a graph has
a self-dual embedding in a non-orientable surface if it has a {Ka : a вүҘ 4}-decomposition. Since
every graph is {K4 , K5 , K6 }-divisible, say, Theorem 1.6 implies that almost every graph has a
{K4 , K5 , K6 }-decomposition and thus a self-dual embedding.

1.5. Matchings and further results. As another illustration, we now state a consequence of
our main result which concerns perfect matchings in hypergraphs that satisfy certain uniformity
conditions on their edge distribution. Note that the conditions are much weaker than any standard
pseudorandomness notion.
Theorem 1.7. For all f вүҘ 2 and Оҫ > 0 there exists n0 вҲҲ N such that the following holds whenever
n вүҘ n0 and f | n. Let G be a f -graph on n vertices which satisfies the following properties:
     вҖў for some d вүҘ Оҫ, |G(v)| = (d Вұ 0.01Оҫ)nf вҲ’1 for all v вҲҲ V (G);
                                                            (f )
     вҖў every vertex is contained in at least Оҫnf copies of Kf +1 ;
     вҖў |G(v) вҲ© G(w)| вүҘ Оҫnf вҲ’1 for all v, w вҲҲ V (G).
Then G has at least 0.01Оҫnf вҲ’1 edge-disjoint perfect matchings.
                       (f )                                                                    (f )
   Note that for G = Kn , this is strengthened by BaranyaiвҖҷs theorem [4], which states that Kn
has a decomposition into nвҲ’1f вҲ’1 edge-disjoint perfect matchings. More generally, the interplay
between designs and the existence of (almost) perfect matchings in hypergraphs has resulted in
major developments over the past decades, e.g. via the RoМҲdl nibble. For more recent progress on
results concerning perfect matchings in hypergraphs and related topics, see e.g. the surveys [41,
52, 53].
   We discuss further applications of our main result in Section 4, e.g. to partite graphs (see
Example 4.11) and to (n, f, r, О»)-block designs where we allow any О» вүӨ nf вҲ’r /(11 В· 7r f !), say
(under more restrictive divisibility conditions, see Corollary 4.14).
                                                          (r)
1.6. Counting. An approximate F -decomposition of Kn is a set of edge-disjoint copies of F
      (r)                                            (r)
in Kn which together cover almost all edges of Kn . Given good bounds on the number of
                                     (r)
approximate F -decompositions of Kn whose set of leftover edges forms a typical r-graph, one
can apply Theorem 1.1 to obtain corresponding bounds on the number of F -decompositions in
  (r)
Kn (see [23, 24] for the clique case). Such lower bounds on the number of approximate F -
decompositions can be achieved by considering either a random greedy F -removal process or an
associated F -nibble removal process. Linial and Luria [33] developed an entropy-based approach
which they used to obtain good upper bounds e.g. on the number of Steiner triple systems. These
developments also make it possible to systematically study random designs (see Kwan [32] for an
investigation of random Steiner triple systems).
1.7. Outline of the paper. As mentioned earlier, our main result (Theorem 4.7) actually con-
cerns F -decompositions in so-called supercomplexes. We will define supercomplexes in Section 4
and derive Theorems 1.1, 1.2, 1.4, 1.6 and 1.7 in Section 9. The definition of a supercomplex
G involves mainly the distribution of cliques of size f in G (where f = |V (F )|). The notion is
weaker than usual notions of quasirandomness. This has two main advantages: firstly, our proof
is by induction on r, and working with this weaker notion is essential to make the induction
proof work. Secondly, this allows us to deduce Theorems 1.1, 1.2, 1.4, 1.6 and 1.7 from a single
statement.
6                             S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



   However, Theorem 4.7 applies only to F -decompositions of a supercomplex G for weakly regular
r-graphs F (which allows us to deduce Theorem 1.4 but not Theorem 1.1).
   To deal with this, in Section 9 we first provide an explicit construction which shows that every
r-graph F can be вҖҳperfectlyвҖҷ packed into a suitable weakly regular r-graph F вҲ— . In particular, F вҲ—
has an F -decomposition. The idea is then to apply Theorem 4.7 to find an F вҲ— -decomposition
in G. Unfortunately, G may not be F вҲ— -divisible. To overcome this, in Section 11 we show that
we can remove a small set of copies of F from G to achieve that the leftover GвҖІ of G is now F вҲ— -
divisible (see Lemma 9.4 for the statement). This now implies Theorem 1.1 for F -decompositions,
i.e. for О» = 1. However, by repeatedly applying Theorem 4.7 in a suitable way, we can actually
allow О» to be as large as required in Theorem 1.1.
   It thus remains to prove Theorem 4.7 itself. We achieve this via an approach based on вҖҳiterative
absorptionвҖҷ. We give a sketch of the argument in Section 3.
   As a byproduct of the construction of the weakly regular r-graph F вҲ— outlined above, we
prove the existence of resolvable clique decompositions in complete partite r-graphs G (see The-
orem 9.1). The construction is explicit and exploits the property that all square submatrices of
so-called Cauchy matrices over finite fields are invertible. We believe this construction to be of
independent interest. A natural question leading on from the current work would be to obtain
                                                                                                 (2)
such resolvable decompositions also in the general (non-partite) case. For decompositions of Kn
        (2)
into Kf , this is due to Ray-Chaudhuri and Wilson [39]. For related results see [15, 34].

We write A вҲӘВ· B for the union of A and B if we want to emphasise that A and B are disjoint.

   We write x вүӘ y to mean that for any y вҲҲ (0, 1] there exists an x0 вҲҲ (0, 1) such that for all

will often use the fact that for all 0 < x < 1 and n вҲҲ N we have (1 Вұ x)n = 1 Вұ 2n x.
   When dealing with multisets, we treat multiple appearances of the same element as distinct
elements. In particular, two subsets A, B of a multiset can be disjoint even if they both contain
a copy of the same element, and if A and B are disjoint, then the multiplicity of an element in
the union A вҲӘ B is obtained by adding the multiplicities of this element in A and B (rather than
just taking the maximum).

                                  3. Outline of the methods
   Rather than an algebraic approach as in [23], we pursue a combinatorial approach based on
вҖҳiterative absorptionвҖҷ. In particular, we do not make use of any nontrivial algebraic techniques
and results, but rely only on probabilistic tools.
                                                                                (r)
3.1. Iterative absorption. Suppose for simplicity that we aim to find a Kf -decomposition of
a suitable r-graph G. The RoМҲdl nibble (see e.g. [1, 37, 40, 46]) allows us to obtain an approximate
   (r)                                                                (r)
Kf -decomposition of G, i.e. a set of edge-disjoint copies of Kf covering almost all edges of
G. However, one has little control over the resulting uncovered leftover set of edges. The basic
aim of an absorbing approach is to overcome this issue by removing an absorbing structure A
right at the beginning and then applying the RoМҲdl nibble to G вҲ’ A, to obtain an approximate
decomposition with a very small uncovered remainder R. Ideally, A was chosen in such a way
                    (r)
that A вҲӘ R has a Kf -decomposition.
8                             S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



   Such an approach was introduced systematically by RoМҲdl, RucinМҒski and SzemereМҒdi [42] in order
to find spanning structures in graphs and hypergraphs (but actually goes back further than this,
see e.g. Krivelevich [29]). In the context of decompositions, the first results based on an absorbing
approach were obtained in [27, 30]. In contrast to the construction of spanning subgraphs, the
decomposition setting gives rise to the additional challenge that the number of and possible shape
of uncovered remainder graphs R is comparatively large. So in general it is much less clear how to
construct a structure A which can deal with all such possibilities for R (to appreciate this issue,
note that V (R) = V (G) in this scenario).
   The method developed in [27, 30] consisted of an iterative approach: each iteration consists
of an approximate decomposition of the previous leftover, together with a partial absorption (or
вҖҳcleaningвҖҷ) step, which further restricts the structure of the current leftover. In our context, we
carry out this iteration by considering a вҖҳvortexвҖҷ. Such a vortex is a nested sequence V (G) =
U0 вҠҮ U1 вҠҮ В· В· В· вҠҮ Uв„“ , where |Ui |/|Ui+1 | and |Uв„“ | are large but bounded. Crucially, after the ith
iteration, all r-edges belonging to the current leftover Ri will be induced by Ui . In the (i + 1)th
iteration, we make use of a suitable r-graph Hi on Ui which we set aside at the start. We first
apply the RoМҲdl nibble to Ri to obtain a sparse remainder RiвҖІ . We then apply what we refer to
                                            (r)
as the вҖҳCover down lemmaвҖҷ to find a Kf -packing Ki of Hi вҲӘ RiвҖІ so that the remainder Ri+1
consists entirely of r-edges induced by Ui+1 (see Lemma 7.7). Ultimately, we arrive at a leftover
Rв„“ induced by Uв„“ .
   Since |Uв„“ | is bounded, this means there are only a bounded number of possibilities S1 , . . . , Sb
for Rв„“ . This gives a natural approach to the construction of an absorber A for Rв„“ : it suffices to
construct an вҖҳexclusiveвҖҷ absorber Ai for each Si (in the sense that Ai can absorb Si but nothing
else). More precisely, we aim to construct edge-disjoint r-graphs A1 , . . . , Ab so that both Ai and
                   (r)
Ai вҲӘ Si have a Kf -decomposition, and then let A := A1 вҲӘ В· В· В· вҲӘ Ab . Then A вҲӘ Rв„“ must also have
    (r)
a Kf -decomposition.
  Iterative absorption based on vortices was introduced in [19], building on a related (but more
complicated approach) in [7]. Developing the above approach in the setting of hypergraph de-
compositions gives rise to two main challenges: constructing the вҖҳexclusiveвҖҷ absorbers and proving
the Cover down lemma, which we discuss in the next two subsections, respectively.
  One difficulty with the iteration process is that after finishing one iteration, the error terms are
too large to carry out the next one. Fortunately, we are able to вҖҳboostвҖҷ our regularity parameters
before each iteration by excluding suitable f -cliques from future consideration (see Lemma 6.3).
For this, we adopt gadgets introduced in [6]. Moreover, the вҖҳBoost lemmaвҖҷ enables us to obtain
explicit bounds e.g. in the minimum degree version (Theorem 1.4).


3.2. The Cover down lemma. As indicated above, the goal here is as follows: Given an r-
graph G and vertex sets Ui+1 вҠҶ Ui in G, we need to construct H вҲ— in G[Ui ](r) so that for any
                                           (r)
sparse leftover R on Ui , we can find a Kf -packing in H вҲ— вҲӘ R such that any leftover edges lie in
Ui+1 . (In addition, we need to ensure that the distribution of the leftover edges within Ui+1 is
sufficiently well-behaved so that we can continue with the next iteration, but we do not discuss
this aspect here.)
    We achieve this goal in several stages: given an edge e вҲҲ H вҲ— вҲӘ R, we refer to the size of its
intersection with Ui+1 as its type. Initially, we cover all edges of type 0. This can be done using
an appropriate greedy approach, i.e. for each edge e of type 0 in turn, we extend e to a copy of
   (r)
Kf using edges of H вҲ— . In the next stage, we cover all edges of type 1, then all edges of type 2
up to and including type r вҲ’ 1. When covering a given set of edges of type j, we will inductively
assume that our main decomposition result holds for j-graphs (note that j < r). For example,
consider the triangle case f = 3 and r = 2, and suppose j = 1. Then for each vertex v вҲҲ Ui \Ui+1 ,
                                                                              (1)
we will inductively find a perfect matching (which can be viewed as a K2 -decomposition) on
the neighbours of v in Ui+1 . This yields a triangle packing which covers all (remaining) edges
incident to v (note that these edges have type 1). The resulting proof of the Cover down lemma
is given in Section 10 (which also includes a more detailed sketch of this part of the argument).
                                                                                                        9



3.3. Transformers and absorbers. Recall that our remaining goal is to construct an exclusive
absorber AS for a given вҖҳleftoverвҖҷ r-graph S of bounded size. In other words, both AS вҲӘ S as
                              (r)
well as AS need to have a Kf -decomposition. Clearly, we must (and can) assume that S is
  (r)
Kf -divisible.
   Based on an idea introduced in [7], we will construct AS as a concatenation of вҖҳtransformersвҖҷ:
given S, a transformer TS can be viewed as transforming S into a new leftover L (which has
the same number of edges and is still divisible). Formally, we require that S вҲӘ TS and TS вҲӘ L
                 (r)
both have a Kf -decomposition (and will set aside TS and L at the beginning of the proof).
Since transformers act transitively, the idea is to concatenate them in order to transform S into a
                              (r)
vertex-disjoint union of Kf , i.e. we gradually transform the given leftover S into a graph which
is trivially decomposable.
   Roughly speaking, we approach this by choosing L to be a suitable вҖҳcanonicalвҖҷ graph (i.e. L
                                                                              (r)
only depends on |S|). Let S вҖІ denote the vertex-disjoint union of copies of Kf such that |S| = |S вҖІ |,
and let TS вҖІ be the corresponding transformer from S вҖІ into L. Then it is easy to see that we could
let AS := TS вҲӘ L вҲӘ TS вҖІ вҲӘ S вҖІ . The construction of both the canonical graph L as well as that of the
transformer TS is based on an inductive approach, i.e. we assume that our main decomposition
result holds for r вҖІ -graphs with 1 вүӨ r вҖІ < r. The above construction is given in Section 8.

                            4. Decompositions of supercomplexes
4.1. Supercomplexes. We prove our main decomposition theorem for so-called вҖҳsupercom-
plexesвҖҷ. The crucial property appearing in the definition is that of вҖҳregularityвҖҷ, which means
that every r-set of a given complex G is contained in roughly the same number of f -sets (where
f = |V (F )|). If we view G as a complex which is induced by some r-graph, this means that every
edge lies in roughly the same number of cliques of size f . It turns out that this set of conditions
is appropriate even when F is not a clique.
   A key advantage of the notion of a supercomplex is that the conditions are very flexible, which
will enable us to вҖҳboostвҖҷ their parameters (see Lemma 4.4 below).
Definition 4.1. Let G be a complex on n vertices, f вҲҲ N and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]0 , 0 вүӨ Оө, d, Оҫ вүӨ 1. We
say that G is
    (i) (Оө, d, f, r)-regular, if for all e вҲҲ G(r) we have
                                        |G(f ) (e)| = (d Вұ Оө)nf вҲ’r ;

   (ii) (Оҫ, f, r)-dense, if for all e вҲҲ G(r) , we have
                                           |G(f ) (e)| вүҘ Оҫnf вҲ’r ;
   (iii) (Оҫ, f, r)-extendable, if G(r)
                                     is empty or there exists a subset X вҠҶ V (G) with |X| вүҘ Оҫn
         such that for all e вҲҲ Xr , there are at least Оҫnf вҲ’r (f вҲ’ r)-sets Q вҠҶ V (G) \ e such that
          QвҲӘe
            r    \ {e} вҠҶ G(r) .
We say that G is a full (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-complex if G is
       вҖў (Оө, d, f, r)-regular for some d вүҘ Оҫ,
       вҖў (Оҫ, f + r, r)-dense,
       вҖў (Оҫ, f, r)-extendable.
We say that G is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-complex if there exists an f -graph Y on V (G) such that G[Y ] is
a full (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-complex. Note that G[Y ](r) = G(r) (recall that r < f ).
   The additional flexibility offered by considering (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-complexes rather than full (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-
complexes is key to proving our minimum degree result (via the вҖҳboostingвҖҷ step discussed below).
We also note that for the scope of this paper, it would be sufficient to define extendability more
restrictively, by letting X := V (G). However, for future applications, it might turn out to be
useful that we do not require X = V (G).
10                             S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



Fact 4.2. Note that G is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, 0)-complex if and only if G is empty or |G(f ) | вүҘ Оҫnf . In
particular, every (Оө, Оҫ, f, 0)-complex is a (0, Оҫ, f, 0)-complex.
Definition 4.3. (supercomplex) Let G be a complex. We say that G is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex
if for every i вҲҲ [r]0 and every set B вҠҶ G(i) with 1 вүӨ |B| вүӨ 2i , we have that bвҲҲB G(b) is an

(Оө, Оҫ, f вҲ’ i, r вҲ’ i)-complex.
    In particular, taking i = 0 and B = {вҲ…} implies that every (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex is also
an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-complex. Moreover, the above definition ensures that if G is a supercomplex and
b, bвҖІ вҲҲ G(i) , then G(b) вҲ© G(bвҖІ ) is also a supercomplex (cf. Proposition 5.5).
    In Section 4.3, we will give some examples of supercomplexes. As mentioned above, the follow-
ing lemma allows us to вҖҳboostвҖҷ the regularity parameters (and thus deduce results with вҖҳeffectiveвҖҷ
bounds). It is an easy consequence of our Boost lemma (Lemma 6.3). The key to the proof is
that we can (probabilistically) choose some Y вҠҶ G(f ) so that the parameters of G[Y ] in Defini-
tion 4.1(i) are better than those of G, i.e. the resulting distribution of f -sets is more uniform.

4.2. The main complex decomposition theorem. The statement of our main complex de-
composition theorem involves the concept of вҖҳwell separatedвҖҷ decompositions. This is crucial for
our inductive proof to work in the context of F -decompositions.
Definition 4.5 (well separated). Let F be an r-graph and let F be an F -packing (in some
r-graph G). We say that F is Оә-well separated if the following hold:
(WS1) for all distinct F вҖІ , F вҖІвҖІ вҲҲ F, we have |V (F вҖІ ) вҲ© V (F вҖІвҖІ )| вүӨ r.
(WS2) for every r-set e, the number of F вҖІ вҲҲ F with e вҠҶ V (F вҖІ ) is at most Оә.
We simply say that F is well separated if (WS1) holds.
                         (r)
   For instance, any Kf -packing is automatically 1-well separated. Moreover, if an F -packing
F is 1-well separated, then for all distinct F вҖІ , F вҖІвҖІ вҲҲ F, we have |V (F вҖІ ) вҲ© V (F вҖІвҖІ )| < r. On the
other hand, since F might not be complete, we do not require |V (F вҖІ ) вҲ© V (F вҖІвҖІ )| < r in (WS1)
                                                                                         (r)
as this would make it impossible to find a well separated F -decomposition of Kn . The notion
of being well-separated is a natural relaxation of this requirement, we discuss this in more detail
after stating Theorem 4.7.
   We now define F -divisibility and F -decompositions for complexes G (rather than r-graphs G).
Definition 4.6. Let F be an r-graph and f := |V (F )|. A complex G is F -divisible if G(r) is
F -divisible. An F -packing in G is an F -packing F in G(r) such that V (F вҖІ ) вҲҲ G(f ) for all F вҖІ вҲҲ F.
Similarly, we say that F is an F -decomposition of G if F is an F -packing in G and F (r) = G(r) .
   Note that this implies that every copy F вҖІ of F used in an F -packing in G is вҖҳsupportedвҖҷ by a
                                (r)
clique, i.e. G(r) [V (F вҖІ )] вҲј
                             = Kf .

   We now motivate Definitions 4.5 and 4.6. This involves the following additional concepts,
which are also convenient later.

Definition 4.8. Let f := |V (F )| and suppose that F is a well separated F -packing. We let F вүӨ

   Note that if F is a well-separated F -packing, then the f -graph {V (F вҖІ ) : F вҖІ вҲҲ F} is simple.

Clearly, we have F (r) вҠҶ F вүӨ(r) , but in general equality does not hold. On the other hand, if F is
an F -decomposition of G, then F (r) = G(r) which implies F (r) = F вүӨ(r) .
   We now discuss (WS1). During our proof, we will need to find an F -packing which covers a
given set of edges. This gives rise to the following task of вҖҳcovering down locallyвҖҷ.
   (вӢҶ) Given a set S вҠҶ V (G) of size 1 вүӨ i вүӨ r вҲ’ 1, find an F -packing F which covers all edges of

   (This is crucial in the proof of the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7). Moreover, a two-sided
version of this involving sets S, S вҖІ is needed to construct parts of our absorbers, see Section 8.1.)
   A natural approach to achieve (вӢҶ) is as follows: Let T вҲҲ V (F            i

                                                                                  . Suppose that by using the
main theorem inductively, we can find an F (T )-decomposition F вҖІ of G(S). We now wish to
obtain F by вҖҳextendingвҖҷ F вҖІ as follows: For each copy F вҖІ of F (T ) in F вҖІ , we define a copy FвҠівҖІ of F
by вҖҳadding S backвҖҷ, that is, FвҠівҖІ has vertex set V (F вҖІ ) вҲӘ S and S plays the role of T in FвҠівҖІ . Then
FвҠівҖІ covers all edges e with S вҠҶ e and e \ S вҲҲ F вҖІ . Since F вҖІ is an F (T )-decomposition of G(S),
the union of all FвҠівҖІ would indeed cover all edges of G that contain S, as desired. There are two
issues with this вҖҳextensionвҖҷ though. Firstly, it is not clear that FвҠівҖІ is a subgraph of G. Secondly,
for distinct F вҖІ , F вҖІвҖІ вҲҲ F вҖІ , it is not clear that FвҠівҖІ and FвҠівҖІвҖІ are edge-disjoint. Definition 4.6 (and the
succeeding remark) allows us to resolve the first issue. Indeed, if F вҖІ is an F (T )-decomposition of
the complex G(S), then from V (F вҖІ ) вҲҲ G(S)(f вҲ’i) , we can deduce V (FвҠівҖІ ) вҲҲ G(f ) and thus that FвҠівҖІ
is a subgraph of G(r) .
   We now consider the second issue. This does not arise if F is a clique. Indeed, in that case
                          (rвҲ’i)
F (T ) is a copy of Kf вҲ’i , and thus for distinct F вҖІ , F вҖІвҖІ вҲҲ F вҖІ we have |V (F вҖІ ) вҲ© V (F вҖІвҖІ )| < r вҲ’ i.
Hence |V (FвҠівҖІ ) вҲ© V (FвҠівҖІвҖІ )| < r вҲ’ i + |S| = r, i.e. FвҠівҖІ and FвҠівҖІвҖІ are edge-disjoint. If however F is not a
clique, then F вҖІ , F вҖІвҖІ вҲҲ F вҖІ can overlap in r вҲ’ i or more vertices (they could in fact have the same
vertex set), and the above argument does not work. We will show that under the assumption
that F вҖІ is well separated, we can overcome this issue and still carry out the above вҖҳextensionвҖҷ.
(Moreover, the resulting F -packing F will in fact be well separated itself, see Definition 7.8 and
Proposition 7.9). For this it is useful to note that F (T ) is an (r вҲ’ i)-graph, and thus we already
have |V (F вҖІ ) вҲ© V (F вҖІвҖІ )| вүӨ r вҲ’ i if F вҖІ is well separated.
   The reason why we also include (WS2) in Definition 4.5 is as follows. Suppose we have already
found a well separated F -packing F1 in G and now want to find another well separated F -packing
                                                                             (r)        (r)      (r)
F2 such that we can combine F1 and F2 . If we find F2 in G вҲ’ F1 , then F1 and F2 are edge-
disjoint and thus F1 вҲӘ F2 will be an F -packing in G, but it is not necessarily well separated. We
                                  (r)     вүӨ(r+1)
therefore find F2 in G вҲ’ F1 вҲ’ F1                 . This ensures that F1 and F2 are (r + 1)-disjoint, which
in turn implies that F1 вҲӘ F2 is indeed well separated, as required. But in order to be able to
                                                     (r)    вүӨ(r+1)
construct F2 , we need to ensure that G вҲ’ F1 вҲ’ F1                   is still a supercomplex, which is true if
     (r)               вүӨ(r+1)
вҲҶ(F1 ) and вҲҶ(F1                ) are small (cf. Proposition 5.9). The latter in turn is ensured by (WS2)
via Fact 5.4.
   Finally, we discuss why we prove Theorem 4.7 for weakly regular r-graphs F . Most import-
antly, the вҖҳregularityвҖҷ of the degrees will be crucial for the construction of our absorbers (most
notably in Lemma 8.25). Beyond that, weakly regular graphs also have useful closure properties
(cf. Proposition 5.3): they are closed under taking link graphs and divisibility is inherited by link
graphs in a natural way.
   We prove Theorem 4.7 in Sections 6вҖ“8 and 9.1. As described in Section 1.7, we generalise this
to arbitrary F via Lemma 9.2 (proved in Section 9.2) and Lemma 9.4 (proved in Section 11):
Lemma 9.2 shows that for every given r-graph F , there is a weakly regular r-graph F вҲ— which
12                                S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



has an F -decomposition. Lemma 9.4 then complements this by showing that every F -divisible r-
graph G can be transformed into an F вҲ— -divisible r-graph GвҖІ by removing a sparse F -decomposable
subgraph of G.
4.3. Applications. As the definition of a supercomplex covers a broad range of settings, we
give some applications here. We will use Examples 4.9, 4.10 and 4.12 in Section 9 to prove
Theorems 1.1, 1.2, 1.4, 1.6 and 1.7. We will also see that random subcomplexes of a supercomplex
are again supercomplexes with appropriately adjusted parameters (see Corollary 5.19).

Example 4.11 (Partite graphs). Let 1/N вүӘ 1/k and 2 = r < f вүӨ k вҲ’6. Let V1 , . . . , Vk be vertex
sets of size N each. Let G be the complete k-partite 2-graph on V1 , . . . , Vk . It is straightforward
to check that GвҶ” is a (0, kвҲ’f , f, 2)-supercomplex. Thus, using Theorem 4.7, we can deduce that
G has an F -decomposition if it is F -divisible. To obtain a minimum degree version (and more
generally, a resilience version) along the lines of Theorems 1.4 and 9.3, one can argue similarly
as in the proof of Theorem 9.3 (cf. Section 9).
   Results on (fractional) decompositions of dense f -partite 2-graphs into f -cliques are proved
in [8, 10, 35]. These have applications to the completion of partial (mutually orthogonal) Latin
squares.

Fact 5.6. If G is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex, then for all distinct e, eвҖІ вҲҲ G(r) , we have |G(f ) (e) вҲ©

   In what follows, we gather tools that show that supercomplexes are robust with respect to small
perturbations. We first bound the number of f -sets that can affect a given edge e. We provide
two bounds, one that we use when optimising our bounds (e.g. in the derivation of Theorem 1.4)
and a more convenient one that we use when the precise value of the parameters is irrelevant
(e.g. in the proof of Proposition 5.9).

5.3. Probabilistic tools. The following Chernoff-type bounds form the basis of our concentra-
tion results that we use for probabilistic arguments.
Lemma 5.10 (see [22, Corollary 2.3, Corollary 2.4, Remark 2.5 and Theorem 2.8]). Let X be
the sum of n independent Bernoulli random variables. Then the following hold.
                                               2
     (i) For all t вүҘ 0, P(|X вҲ’ EX| вүҘ t) вүӨ 2eвҲ’2t /n .
                                                      2

   (iii) If t вүҘ 7EX, then P(X вүҘ t) вүӨ eвҲ’t .
     We will also use the following simple result.
Proposition 5.11 (Jain, see [38, Lemma 8]). Let X1 , . . . , Xn be Bernoulli random variables such
that, for any i вҲҲ [n] and any x1 , . . . , xiвҲ’1 вҲҲ {0, 1},
                              P(Xi = 1 | X1 = x1 , . . . , XiвҲ’1 = xiвҲ’1 ) вүӨ p.

  Similarly as in [20], Lemma 5.12 can be conveniently applied in the following situation: We

Fact 5.13. Every r-graph on n vertices can be decomposed into rnrвҲ’1 matchings.

   Whenever we apply Corollary 5.14, it will be clear that for every matching M in H, the edges
of M survive independently, and we will not discuss this explicitly.

5.4. Random subsets and subgraphs. In this subsection, we apply the above tools to obtain
basic results about random subcomplexes. The first one deals with taking a random subset of
the vertex set, and the second one considers the complex obtained by randomly sparsifying G(r) .

5.5. Rooted Embeddings. We now prove a result (Lemma 5.20) which allows us to find edge-
disjoint embeddings of graphs with a prescribed вҖҳroot embeddingвҖҷ. Let T be an r-graph and
suppose that X вҠҶ V (T ) is such that T [X] is empty. A root of (T, X) is a set S вҠҶ X with
|S| вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1] and |T (S)| > 0.
   For an r-graph G, we say that Оӣ : X вҶ’ V (G) is a G-labelling of (T, X) if Оӣ is injective. Our aim
is to embed T into G such that the roots of (T, X) are embedded at their assigned position. More
precisely, given a G-labelling Оӣ of (T, X), we say that ПҶ is a Оӣ-faithful embedding of (T, X) into
G if ПҶ is an injective homomorphism from T to G with ПҶвҶҫX = Оӣ. Moreover, for a set S вҠҶ V (G)
with |S| вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1], we say that Оӣ roots S if S вҠҶ Im(Оӣ) and |T (ОӣвҲ’1 (S))| > 0, i.e. if ОӣвҲ’1 (S) is a
root of (T, X).
   The degeneracy of T rooted at X is the smallest D such that there exists an ordering v1 , . . . , vk
of the vertices of V (T ) \ X such that for every в„“ вҲҲ [k], we have
                                       |T [X вҲӘ {v1 , . . . , vв„“ }](vв„“ )| вүӨ D,
i.e. every vertex is contained in at most D edges which lie to the left of that vertex in the ordering.
   We need to be able to embed many copies of (T, X) simultaneously (with different labellings)
into a given host graph G such that the different embeddings are edge-disjoint. In fact, we need a
slightly stronger disjointness criterion. Ideally, we would like to have that two distinct embeddings
intersect in less than r vertices. However, this is in general not possible because of the desired
rooting. We therefore introduce the following concept of a hull. We will ensure that the hulls are
edge-disjoint, which will be sufficient for our purposes. Given (T, X) as above, the hull of (T, X)
is the r-graph T вҖІ on V (T ) with e вҲҲ T вҖІ if and only if e вҲ© X = вҲ… or e вҲ© X is a root of (T, X).
                         (r)       (r)          (r)
Note that T вҠҶ T вҖІ вҠҶ KV (T ) вҲ’ KX , where KZ denotes the complete r-graph with vertex set Z.
Moreover, the roots of (T вҖІ , X) are precisely the roots of (T, X).

                           6. Nibbles, boosting and greedy covers
6.1. The nibble. There are numerous results based on the RoМҲdl nibble which guarantee the
existence of an almost perfect matching in a near regular hypergraph with smallcodegrees. Our
application of this is as follows: Let G be a complex. Define the auxiliary fr -graph H with
V (H) = E(G(r) ) and E(H) = { Qr : Q вҲҲ G(f ) }. Note that for every e вҲҲ V (H), |H(e)| =
                                           

|G(f ) (e)|. Thus, if G is (Оө, d, f, r)-regular, then every vertex of H has degree (dВұОө)nf вҲ’r . Moreover,
for two vertices e, eвҖІ вҲҲ V (H), we have |H({e, eвҖІ })| вүӨ nf вҲ’rвҲ’1 , thus вҲҶ2 (H) вүӨ nf вҲ’rвҲ’1 . Standard
nibble theorems would in this setting imply the existence of an almost perfect matching in H,
                               (r)
which translates into a Kf -packing in G that covers all but o(nr ) r-edges. We need a stronger
result in the sense that we want the leftover r-edges to induce an r-graph with small maximum
degree. Alon and Yuster [2] observed that one can use a result of Pippenger and Spencer [37] (on
the chromatic index of uniform hypergraphs) to show that a near regular hypergraph with small
codegrees has an almost perfect matching which is вҖҳwell-behavedвҖҷ. The following is an immediate
consequence of Theorem 1.2 in [2] (applied to the auxiliary hypergraph H above).
Theorem 6.1 ([2]). Let 1/n вүӘ Оө вүӘ Оі, d, 1/f and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]. Suppose that G is an (Оө, d, f, r)-
                                                  (r)
regular complex on n vertices. Then G contains a Kf -packing K such that вҲҶ(G(r) вҲ’ K(r) ) вүӨ Оіn.
6.2. The Boost lemma. We will now state and prove the вҖҳBoost lemmaвҖҷ, which вҖҳboostsвҖҷ the
regularity of a complex by restricting to a suitable set Y of f -sets. It will help us to keep the error
terms under control during the iteration process and also helps us to obtain meaningful resilience
and minimum degree bounds.
   The proof is based on the following вҖҳedge-gadgetsвҖҷ, which were used in [6] to obtain fractional
  (r)
Kf -decompositions of r-graphs with high minimum degree. These edge-gadgets allow us to
locally adjust a given weighting of f -sets so that this changes the total weight at only one r-set.
Proposition 6.2 (see [6, Proposition 3.3]). Let f > r вүҘ 1 and let e and J be disjoint sets with
|e| = r and |J| = f . Let G be the complete complex on eвҲӘ J. There exists a function ПҲ : G(f ) вҶ’ R
such that                                          (

reasonable Оө and consider a uniform weighting of all f -sets. We then use the edge-gadgets to shift

role of G). This yields Y вҖІ вҠҶ Y such that G[Y вҖІ ] is (nвҲ’1/3 , d/2, f, r)-regular and (Оҫ вҖІ , f + r, r)-dense.

6.3. Approximate F -decompositions. We now prove an F -nibble lemma which allows us to
find Оә-well separated approximate F -decompositions in supercomplexes. Whenever we need an
approximate decomposition in the proof of Theorem 4.7, we will obtain it via Lemma 6.5.
Lemma 6.5 (F -nibble lemma). Let 1/n вүӘ 1/Оә вүӘ Оі, Оө вүӘ Оҫ, 1/f and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]. Let F be an
r-graph on f vertices. Let G be a complex on n vertices such that G is (Оө, d, f, r)-regular and
(Оҫ, f + r, r)-dense for some d вүҘ Оҫ. Then G contains a Оә-well separated F -packing F such that
вҲҶ(G(r) вҲ’ F (r) ) вүӨ Оіn.
                                                                                                                (r)
   Let F be an r-graph on f vertices. Given a collection K of edge-disjoint copies of Kf , we define
the K-random F -packing F as follows: For every K вҲҲ K, choose a random bijection from V (F ) to
V (K) and let FK be a copy of F on V (K) embedded by this bijection. Let F := {FK : K вҲҲ K}.
                         (r)
   Clearly, if K is a Kf -decomposition of a complex G, then the K-random F -packing F is a
1-well separated F -packing in G. Moreover, writing p := 1 вҲ’ |F |/ fr , we have |F (r) | = |F ||K| =
                                                                         

|F ||G(r) |/ fr = (1 вҲ’ p)|G(r) |, and for every e вҲҲ G(r) , we have P(e вҲҲ G(r) вҲ’ F (r) ) = p. As it turns
               

out, the leftover G(r) вҲ’ F (r) behaves essentially like a p-random subgraph of G(r) (cf. Lemma 6.6).
                                                                                                     (r)
Our strategy to prove Lemma 6.5 is thus as follows: We apply Lemma 6.4 to G to obtain a Kf -
                                              (r)
packing K1 such that вҲҶ(G(r) вҲ’ K1 ) вүӨ Оіn. The leftover here is negligible, so assume for the
                     (r)
moment that K1 is a Kf -decomposition. We then choose a K1 -random F -packing F1 in G and
                                         (r)
continue the process with G вҲ’ F1 . In each step, the leftover decreases by a factor of p. Thus
after logp Оі steps, the leftover will have maximum degree at most Оіn.

                вҲҡ

   We can conveniently combine Lemma 6.5 and Corollary 6.9 to deduce the following result.
It allows us to make an r-graph divisible by deleting a small fraction of edges (even if we are

Section 11 under different assumptions.

                                            7. Vortices
   A vortex is best thought of as a sequence of nested вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ subsets of the vertex set of a
supercomplex G. In our approach, the final set of the vortex has bounded size.
   The main results of this section are Lemmas 7.4 and 7.5, where the first one shows that vortices
exist, and the latter one shows that given a vortex, we can find an F -packing covering all edges
which do not lie inside the final vortex set. We now give the formal definition of what it means
to be a вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ subset.
Definition 7.1. Let G be a complex on n vertices. We say that U is (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r)-random in G
if there exists an f -graph Y on V (G) such that the following hold:
   (R1) U вҠҶ V (G) with |U | = Вөn Вұ n2/3 ;
   (R2) there exists d вүҘ Оҫ such that for all x вҲҲ [f вҲ’ r]0 and all e вҲҲ G(r) , we have that
                |{Q вҲҲ G[Y ](f ) (e) : |Q вҲ© U | = x}| = (1 Вұ Оө)bin(f вҲ’ r, Вө, x)dnf вҲ’r ;

  (R3) for all e вҲҲ G(r) we have |G[Y ](f +r) (e)[U ]| вүҘ Оҫ(Вөn)f ;
  (R4) for all h вҲҲ [r]0 and all B вҠҶ G(h) with 1 вүӨ |B| вүӨ 2h we have that bвҲҲB G(b)[U ] is an
                                                                       T
       (Оө, Оҫ, f вҲ’ h, r вҲ’ h)-complex.
  We record the following easy consequences for later use.
Fact 7.2. The following hold.
    (i) If G is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex, then V (G) is (Оө/Оҫ, 1, Оҫ, f, r)-random in G.
   (ii) If U is (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r)-random in G, then G[U ] is an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex.
   Here, (ii) follows immediately from (R4). Note that (R4) is stronger in the sense that B is not
restricted to U . Having defined what it means to be a вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ subset, we can now define
what a vortex is.
Definition 7.3 (Vortex). Let G be a complex. An (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r, m)-vortex in G is a sequence
U0 вҠҮ U1 вҠҮ В· В· В· вҠҮ Uв„“ such that
 (V1) U0 = V (G);
 (V2) |Ui | = вҢҠВө|UiвҲ’1 |вҢӢ for all i вҲҲ [в„“];
 (V3) |Uв„“ | = m;
 (V4) for all i вҲҲ [в„“], Ui is (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r)-random in G[UiвҲ’1 ];
 (V5) for all i вҲҲ [в„“ вҲ’ 1], Ui \ Ui+1 is (Оө, Вө(1 вҲ’ Вө), Оҫ, f, r)-random in G[UiвҲ’1 ].
  We will show in Section 7.2 that a vortex can be found in a supercomplex by repeatedly taking
random subsets.
30                             S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



Lemma 7.4. Let 1/mвҖІ вүӘ Оө вүӘ Вө, Оҫ, 1/f such that Вө вүӨ 1/2  вҲҡ and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]. Let G be an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-
supercomplex on n вүҘ mвҖІ vertices. Then there exists a (2 Оө, Вө, Оҫ вҲ’ Оө, f, r, m)-vortex in G for some
ВөmвҖІ вүӨ m вүӨ mвҖІ .
  The following is the main lemma of this section. Given a vortex in a supercomplex G, it allows
us to cover all edges of G(r) except possibly some from inside the final vortex set. We will prove
Lemma 7.5 in Section 7.4.
Lemma 7.5. Let 1/m вүӘ 1/Оә вүӘ Оө вүӘ Вө вүӘ Оҫ, 1/f and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]. Assume that (вҲ—)k is true
for all k вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1]. Let F be a weakly regular r-graph on f vertices. Let G be an F -divisible
(Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex and U0 вҠҮ U1 вҠҮ В· В· В· вҠҮ Uв„“ an (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r, m)-vortex in G. Then there
exists a 4Оә-well separated F -packing F in G which covers all edges of G(r) except possibly some
inside Uв„“ .
   The proof of Lemma 7.5 consists of an вҖҳiterative absorptionвҖҷ procedure, where the key ingredient
is the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7). Roughly speaking, given a supercomplex G and a
вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ subset U вҠҶ V (G), the Cover down lemma allows us to find a вҖҳpartial absorberвҖҷ
H вҠҶ G(r) such that for any sparse L вҠҶ G(r) , H вҲӘ L has an F -packing which covers all edges
of H вҲӘ L except possibly some inside U . Together with the F -nibble lemma (Lemma 6.5), this
allows us to cover all edges of G except possibly some inside U whilst using only few edges
inside U . Indeed, set aside H as above, which is reasonably sparse. Then apply the Lemma 6.5
to G вҲ’ G(r) [U ] вҲ’ H to obtain an F -packing Fnibble with a very sparse leftover L. Combine H and
L to find an F -packing Fclean whose leftover lies inside U .
   Now, if U0 вҠҮ U1 вҠҮ В· В· В· вҠҮ Uв„“ is a vortex, then U1 is вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ in G and thus we can cover
all edges which are not inside U1 by using only few edges inside U1 (and in this step we forbid
edges inside U2 from being used.) Then U2 is still вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ in the remainder of G[U1 ], and
hence we can iterate until we have covered all edges of G except possibly some inside Uв„“ .
7.1. The Cover down lemma. We now provide the formal statement of the Cover down lemma.
We will prove it in Section 10.
Definition 7.6. Let G be a complex on n vertices and H вҠҶ G(r) . We say that G is (Оҫ, f, r)-dense
with respect to H if for all e вҲҲ G(r) , we have |G[H вҲӘ {e}](f ) (e)| вүҘ Оҫnf вҲ’r .
Lemma 7.7 (Cover down lemma). Let 1/n вүӘ 1/Оә вүӘ Оі вүӘ Оө вүӘ ОҪ вүӘ Вө, Оҫ, 1/f and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1] with
Вө вүӨ 1/2. Assume that (вҲ—)i is true for all i вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1] and that F is a weakly regular r-graph on f
vertices. Let G be a complex on n vertices and suppose that U is (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r)-random in G. Let
GМғ be a complex on V (G) with G вҠҶ GМғ such that GМғ is (Оө, f, r)-dense with respect to G(r) вҲ’ G(r) [UМ„ ],
where UМ„ := V (G) \ U .
   Then there exists a subgraph H вҲ— вҠҶ G(r) вҲ’ G(r) [UМ„ ] with вҲҶ(H вҲ— ) вүӨ ОҪn such that for any L вҠҶ GМғ(r)
with вҲҶ(L) вүӨ Оіn and H вҲ— вҲӘ L being F -divisible and any (r + 1)-graph O on V (G) with вҲҶ(O) вүӨ Оіn,
there exists a Оә-well separated F -packing in GМғ[H вҲ— вҲӘ L] вҲ’ O which covers all edges of H вҲ— вҲӘ L except
possibly some inside U .
   Roughly speaking, the proof of the Cover down lemma proceeds as follows. Suppose that we
have already chosen H вҲ— and that L is any sparse (leftover) r-graph. For an edge e вҲҲ H вҲ— вҲӘ L, we
refer to |e вҲ© U | as its type. Since L is very sparse, we can greedily cover all edges of L using edges
of H вҲ— in a first step. In particular, this covers all type-0-edges. We will now continue     and cover
all type-1-edges. Note that every type-1-edge contains a unique S вҲҲ V (G)\U
                                                                                    
                                                                               rвҲ’1   .  For a  given set
       V (G)\U                                                      вҲ—
S вҲҲ      rвҲ’1     , we would like to cover all remaining edges of H that contain S simultaneously.
Assuming a suitable choice of H вҲ— , this can be achieved as follows. Let LS be the link graph
of S after the first step. Let T вҲҲ VrвҲ’1   (F )

Proposition 7.9 below implies that we can вҖҳextendвҖҷ FSвҖІ to a Оә-well separated F -packing FS which
covers all edges that contain S.
   However, in order to cover all type-1-edges, we need to obtain such a packing FS for every

F -packing again. The real difficulty thus lies in choosing H вҲ— in such a way that the link graphs LS
do not interfere too much with each other, and then to choose the decompositions FSвҖІ sequentially
(see the discussion in the beginning of Section 10). We would then continue to cover all type-2-
edges using (вҲ—)2 , etc., until we finally cover all type-(rвҲ’1)-edges using (вҲ—)rвҲ’1 . The only remaining
edges are then type-r-edges, which are contained in U , as desired.
   We now show how the notion of well separated F -packings allows us to вҖҳextendвҖҷ a decomposition
of a link complex to a packing which covers all edges that contain a given set S (cf. the discussion
in Section 4.2).

7.3. Existence of cleaners. Recall that the Cover down down lemma guarantees the existence
of a suitable вҖҳcleaning graphвҖҷ or вҖҳpartial absorberвҖҷ which allows us to вҖҳcleanвҖҷ the leftover of an
application of the F -nibble lemma in the sense that the new leftover is guaranteed to lie in the
next vortex set. For technical reasons, we will in fact find all cleaning graphs first (one for each
vortex set) and set them aside even before the first nibble.
   The aim of this subsection is to apply the Cover down lemma to each вҖҳlevelвҖҷ i of the vortex to
obtain a вҖҳcleaning graphвҖҷ Hi (playing the role of H вҲ— ) for each i вҲҲ [в„“] (see Lemma 7.15). Let G be
a complex and U0 вҠҮ U1 вҠҮ В· В· В· вҠҮ Uв„“ a vortex in G. We say that H1 , . . . , Hв„“ is a (Оі, ОҪ, Оә, F )-cleaner
(for the said vortex) if the following hold for all i вҲҲ [в„“]:
  (C1) Hi вҠҶ G(r) [UiвҲ’1 ] вҲ’ G(r) [Ui+1 ], where Uв„“+1 := вҲ…;
  (C2) вҲҶ(Hi ) вүӨ ОҪ|UiвҲ’1 |;
  (C3) Hi and Hi+1 are edge-disjoint, where Hв„“+1 := вҲ…;

                                             8. Absorbers
   In this section we show that for any (divisible) r-graph H in a supercomplex G, we can find
an вҖҳexclusiveвҖҷ absorber r-graph A (as discussed in Section 1.7, one may think of H as a potential
leftover from an approximate F -decomposition and A will be set aside earlier to absorb H into
an F -decomposition). The following definition makes this precise. The main result of this section
is Lemma 8.2, which constructs an absorber provided that F is weakly regular. Building on [7],
we will construct absorbers as a concatenation of вҖҳtransformersвҖҷ and special вҖҳcanonical graphsвҖҷ.
The goal is to transform an arbitrary divisible r-graph H into a canonical graph. In the following
subsection, we will construct transformers. In Section 8.2, we will prove the existence of suitable
canonical graphs. We will prove Lemma 8.2 in Section 8.3.
Definition 8.1 (Absorber). Let F , H and A be r-graphs. We say that A is an F -absorber for H
if A and H are edge-disjoint and both A and A вҲӘ H have an F -decomposition. More generally,
if G is a complex and H вҠҶ G(r) , then A вҠҶ G(r) is a Оә-well separated F -absorber for H in G if A
and H are edge-disjoint and there exist Оә-well separated F -packings Fв—Ұ and FвҖў in G such that
   (r)          (r)
Fв—Ұ = A and FвҖў = A вҲӘ H.
Lemma 8.2 (Absorbing lemma). Let 1/n вүӘ 1/Оә вүӘ Оі, 1/h, Оө вүӘ Оҫ, 1/f and r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1]. Assume
that (вҲ—)i is true for all i вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1]. Let F be a weakly regular r-graph on f vertices, let G be an
(Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex on n vertices and let H be an F -divisible subgraph of G(r) with |H| вүӨ h.
Then there exists a Оә-well separated F -absorber A for H in G with вҲҶ(A) вүӨ Оіn.
   We now briefly discuss the case r = 1. We write V (F ) = {x1 , . . . , xf } and can assume that
F = {{x1 }, . . . , {xt }} for some t вҲҲ [f ].
   Assume first that H = {e1 , . . . , et }. Choose any f -set Q0 вҲҲ G(f ) and write Q0 = {v1 , . . . , vf }.
Let F0 be a copy of F with vertex set Q0 such that F0 = {{v1 }, . . . , {vt }}. Now, for every i вҲҲ [t],
choose a Qi вҲҲ G(f ) (ei ) вҲ© G(f ) ({vi }) (cf. Fact 5.6). Choose these sets such that H, Q0 , . . . , Qt
                                                                                        S
are pairwise disjoint. For every i вҲҲ [t], let Fi and FiвҖІ be copies of F such that V (Fi ) = Qi вҲӘ ei ,
V (FiвҖІ ) = Qi вҲӘ {vi }Sand Fi в–і FiвҖІ = {ei , {vi }}.

Fв—Ұ = A, and FвҖў := {F0 , F1 , . . . , Ft } is a 1-well separated F -packing in G with FвҖў = A вҲӘ H.
Thus, A is a 1-well separated F -absorber for H in G. More generally, if H is any F -divisible
1-graph, then t | |H|, so we can partition the edges of H into |H|/t subgraphs of size t and then
find an absorber for each of these subgraphs (successively so that they are appropriately disjoint.)
Thus, for the remainder of this section, we will assume that r вүҘ 2.
8.1. Transformers. Roughly speaking, a transformer T can be viewed as transforming a given
leftover graph H into a new leftover H вҖІ (where we set aside T and H вҖІ earlier).
Definition 8.3 (Transformer). Let F be an r-graph, G a complex and assume that H, H вҖІ вҠҶ G(r) .
A subgraph T вҠҶ G(r) is a Оә-well separated (H, H вҖІ ; F )-transformer in G if T is edge-disjoint from
both H and H вҖІ and there exist Оә-well separated F -packings F and F вҖІ in G such that F (r) = T вҲӘH
and F вҖІ(r) = T вҲӘ H вҖІ .
   Our вҖҳTransforming lemmaвҖҷ (Lemma 8.5) guarantees the existence of a transformer for H and
H вҖІ if H вҖІ is obtained from H by вҖҳidentifyingвҖҷ vertices.     To make this more precise, given a multi-
r-graph H and x, xвҖІ вҲҲ V (H), we say that x and xвҖІ are identifiable if |H({x, xвҖІ })| = 0, that is, if
identifying x and xвҖІ does not create an edge of size less than r. (Identifying x and xвҖІ means that
we create a new vertex xвҲ— , replace all appearances of x, xвҖІ in edges with xвҲ— , and delete x, xвҖІ .) For
multi-r-graphs H and H вҖІ , we write H         H вҖІ if there is a sequence H0 , . . . , Ht of multi-r-graphs
              вҲј                             вҖІ
such that H0 = H, Ht is obtained from H by deleting isolated vertices, and for every i вҲҲ [t], there
are two identifiable vertices x, xвҖІ вҲҲ V (HiвҲ’1 ) such that Hi is obtained from HiвҲ’1 by identifying x
and xвҖІ .
   If H and H вҖІ are (simple) r-graphs and H        H вҖІ , we just write H   H вҖІ to indicate the fact that

   We now sketch the proof of Lemma 8.5. Suppose for simplicity that H вҖІ is simply a copy of H,
i.e. H вҖІ = ПҶ(H) where ПҶ is an isomorphism from H to H вҖІ . We aim to construct an (H, H вҖІ ; F )-

and R1 := eвҲҲH Fe вҲ’ T1 вҲ’ H. Clearly, {Fe : e вҲҲ H} is an F -decomposition of H вҲӘ R1 вҲӘ T1 . By
Fact 8.7(ii), we also have that {ПҶ(Fe ) : e вҲҲ H} is an F -decomposition of H вҖІ вҲӘ ПҶ(R1 ) вҲӘ T1 . Hence,
T1 is an (H вҲӘ R1 , H вҖІ вҲӘ ПҶ(R1 ); F )-transformer. Note that at this stage, it would suffice to find an
(R1 , ПҶ(R1 ); F )-transformer T1вҖІ , as then T1 вҲӘ T1вҖІ вҲӘ R1 вҲӘ ПҶ(R1 ) would be an (H, H вҖІ ; F )-transformer.
The crucial difference now to the original problem is that every edge of R1 contains at most r вҲ’ 1
vertices from V (H). On the other hand, every edge in R1 contains at least one vertex in V (H) as
otherwise it would belong to T1 . We view this as Step 1 and will now proceed inductively. After
Step i, we will have an r-graph Ri and an (H вҲӘ Ri , H вҖІ вҲӘ ПҶ(Ri ); F )-transformer Ti such that every
edge e вҲҲ Ri satisfies 1 вүӨ |e вҲ© V (H)| вүӨ r вҲ’ i. Thus, after Step r we can terminate the process as
Rr must be empty and thus Tr is an (H, H вҖІ ; F )-transformer.
   In Step i+1, where i вҲҲ [rвҲ’1], we use (вҲ—)i inductively as follows. Let RiвҖІ consist of all edges of Ri
which intersect V (H) in r вҲ’ i vertices. We decompose RiвҖІ into вҖҳlocalвҖҷ parts. For every edge e вҲҲ RiвҖІ ,

  So far, our maps ПҶ : S1 вҶ’ S2 were bijections. When ПҶ is an edge-bijective homomorphism from
H to H вҖІ , ПҶ is in general not injective. In order to still have a meaningful notion of вҖҳmirroringвҖҷ as
before, we introduce the following notation.
Definition 8.11. Let V be a set and let V1 , V2 be disjoint subsets of V , and let ПҶ : V1 вҶ’ V2 be
a map. For a set S вҠҶ V \ V2 , define ПҶ(S) := (S \ V1 ) вҲӘ ПҶ(S вҲ© V1 ). Let r вҲҲ N and suppose that
R is an r-graph with V (R) вҠҶ V and i вҲҲ [r]0 . We say that R is (ПҶ, V, V1 , V2 , i)-projectable if the
following hold:
  (Y1) for every e вҲҲ R, we have that e вҲ© V2 = вҲ… and |e вҲ© V1 | вҲҲ [i] (so if i = 0, then R must be
        empty since [0] = вҲ…);
  (Y2) for every e вҲҲ R, we have |ПҶ(e)| = r;
  (Y3) for every two distinct edges e, eвҖІ вҲҲ R, we have ПҶ(e) 6= ПҶ(eвҖІ ).
Note that if ПҶ is injective and e вҲ© V2 = вҲ… for all e вҲҲ R, then (Y2) and (Y3) always hold. If
R is (ПҶ, V, V1 , V2 , i)-projectable, then let ПҶ(R) be the r-graph on ПҶ(V (R) \ V2 ) with edge set
{ПҶ(e) : e вҲҲ R}. For an r-graph P with V (P ) вҠҶ V \ V2 that satisfies (Y2), let P ПҶ be the r-graph
on V (P ) вҲӘ V1 that consists of all e вҲҲ V \V       such that ПҶ(e) = ПҶ(eвҖІ ) for some eвҖІ вҲҲ P .

8.2. Canonical multi-r-graphs. Roughly speaking, the aim of this section is to show that any
F -divisible r-graph H can be transformed into a canonical multigraph Mh which does not depend
on the structure of H. However, it turns out that for this we need to move to a вҖҳdualвҖҷ setting,
where we consider вҲҮH which is obtained from H by applying an F -extension operator вҲҮ. This
operator allows us to switch between multi-r-graphs (which arise naturally in the construction but
are not present in the complex G we are decomposing) and (simple) r-graphs (see e.g. Fact 8.18).
   Given a multi-r-graph H and a set X of size r, we say that ПҲ is an X-orientation of H if ПҲ is a
collection of bijective maps ПҲe : X вҶ’ e, one for each e вҲҲ H. (For r = 2 and X = {1, 2}, say, this
coincides with the notion of an oriented multigraph, e.g. by viewing ПҲe (1) as the tail and ПҲe (2)
as the head of e, where parallel edges can be oriented in opposite directions.)
   Given an r-graph F and a distinguished edge e0 вҲҲ F , we introduce the following вҖҳextensionвҖҷ
operators вҲҮ Лң (F,e ) and вҲҮ(F,e ) .
                  0           0

Thus, T is an (H, H вҖІ ; F )-transformer (cf. Fact 8.14(i)). Hence, together with (8.13) and Lemma 8.5,
this means that we can transform H into вҲҮMh . Since Mh does not depend on H, we can also
transform the empty r-graph into вҲҮMh , and by transitivity we can transform H into the empty
graph, which amounts to an absorber for H (the detailed proof of this can be found in Section 8.3).
   We now give the rigorous statement of (8.13), which is the main lemma of this subsection.
Lemma 8.15. Let r вүҘ 2 and assume that (вҲ—)i is true for all i вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1]. Let F be a weakly
regular r-graph and e0 вҲҲ F . Then for all h вҲҲ N, there exists a multi-r-graph Mh such that for
any F -divisible r-graph H on at most h vertices, we have
                   вҲҮ(F,e0 ) (вҲҮ(F,e0 ) (H + t В· F, ПҲ1 ) + s В· F, ПҲ3 )   вҲҮ(F,e0) (Mh , ПҲ2 )
for suitable s, t вҲҲ N, where ПҲ1 and ПҲ2 can be arbitrary e0 -orientations of H + t В· F and Mh ,
respectively, and ПҲ3 is an e0 -orientation depending on these.
  The above graphs вҲҮ(вҲҮ(H + t В· F ) + s В· F ) and вҲҮMh will be part of our F -absorber for H.

requirement is formalised by the following definition.

  Before we can prove Lemma 8.15, we need to show the existence of a symmetric r-extender F вҲ—
which is F -decomposable. For some F we could actually take F вҲ— = F (e.g. if F is a clique). For
general (weakly regular) r-graphs F , we will use the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7) to find F вҲ— .
At first sight, appealing to the Cover down lemma may seem rather heavy handed, but a direct
construction seems to be quite difficult.

   Note that |V (F вҲ— )| is quite large here, in particular 1/|V (F вҲ— )| вүӘ 1/f for f = |V (F )|. This
means that G being an (Оө, Оҫ, f, r)-supercomplex does not necessarily allow us to extend a given

in fact not be necessary, as F вҲ— will only serve as an abstract auxiliary graph and will not appear
as a subgraph of the absorber. (This is crucial since otherwise we would not be able to prove our
main theorems with explicit bounds, let alone the bounds given in Theorem 1.4.)

8.3. Proof of the Absorbing lemma. As discussed at the beginning of Section 8.2, we can
now combine Lemma 8.5 and Lemma 8.15 to construct the desired absorber by concatenating
transformers between certain auxiliary r-graphs, in particular the extension вҲҮMh of the canonical
multi-r-graph Mh . It is relatively straightforward to find these auxiliary r-graphs within a given
supercomplex G. The step when we need to find вҲҮMh is the reason why the definition of a
supercomplex includes the notion of extendability.

                                      9. Proof of the main theorems
9.1. Main complex decomposition theorem. We can now deduce our main decomposition
result for supercomplexes (modulo the proof of the Cover down lemma). The main ingredients
for the proof of Theorem 4.7 are Lemma 7.4 (to find a vortex), Lemma 8.2 (to find absorbers for
the possible leftovers in the final vortex set), and Lemma 7.5 (to cover all edges outside the final
vortex set).

9.2. Resolvable partite designs. Perhaps surprisingly, it is much easier to obtain decomposi-
tions of complete partite r-graphs than of complete (non-partite) r-graphs. In fact, we can obtain
(explicit) resolvable decompositions (sometimes referred to as Kirkman systems) in the partite
setting using basic linear algebra. We believe that this result and the corresponding construction
are of independent interest. Here, we will use this result to show that for every r-graph F , there
is a weakly regular r-graph F вҲ— which is F -decomposable (see Lemma 9.2).
                                             (r)
   Let G be a complex. We say that a Kf -decomposition K of G is resolvable if K can be
                         (rвҲ’1)
partitioned into Kf              -decompositions of G, that is, KвүӨ(f ) can be partitioned into sets Y1 , . . . , Yt
                                                                                                        57



                                                                       (rвҲ’1)
such that for each i вҲҲ [t], Ki := {G(rвҲ’1) [Q] : Q вҲҲ Yi } is a Kf         -decomposition of G. Clearly,
K1 , . . . , Kt are r-disjoint.
   Let KnГ—k be the complete k-partite complex with each vertex class having size n. More
precisely, KnГ—k has vertex set V1 вҲӘВ· В· В· В· вҲӘВ· Vk such that |Vi | = n for all i вҲҲ [k] and e вҲҲ KnГ—k if and
only if e is crossing, that is, intersects with each Vi in at most one vertex. Since every subset of
a crossing set is crossing, this defines a complex.
Theorem 9.1. Let q be a prime power and 2f вүӨ q. Then for every r вҲҲ [f вҲ’ 1], KqГ—f has a
            (r)

  Let us first motivate the proof of Theorem 9.1. Let F be the finite field of order q. Assume
that each class of KqГ—f is a copy of F. Suppose further that we are given a matrix A вҲҲ F(f вҲ’r)Г—f
                                                                                       (f )
with the property that every (f вҲ’ r) Г— (f вҲ’ r)-submatrix is invertible. Identifying KqГ—f with
                                                                (f )
Ff in the obvious way, we let K be the set of all Q вҲҲ KqГ—f with AQ = 0. Fixing the entries

which will translate into the fact that every r-set of KqГ—f is contained in exactly one f -set of K,
                  (r)
i.e. we have a Kf -decomposition.
   There are several known classes of matrices over finite fields which have the desired property
that every square submatrix is invertible. We use so-called Cauchy matrices, introduced by
Cauchy [12], which are very convenient for our purposes. For an application of Cauchy matrices
to coding theory, see e.g. [9].
   Let F be a field and let x1 , . . . , xm , y1 , . . . , yn be distinct elements of F. The Cauchy matrix
generated by (xi )iвҲҲ[m] and (yj )jвҲҲ[n] is the m Г— n-matrix A вҲҲ FmГ—n defined by ai,j := (xi вҲ’ yj )вҲ’1 .
Obviously, every submatrix of a Cauchy matrix is itself a Cauchy matrix. For m = n, it is well
known that the Cauchy determinant is given by the following formula (cf. [44]):
                                              Q

                                                           1вүӨi,jвүӨn (xi вҲ’ yj )
In particular, every square Cauchy matrix is invertible.

9.3. Proofs of Theorems 1.1, 1.2, 1.4, 1.6 and 1.7. We now prove our main theorems which

We will also derive Theorems 1.2, 1.6 and 1.7.

proving Theorem 1.4 we actually prove a stronger вҖҳlocal resilience versionвҖҷ. Let Hr (n, p) denote
