                                           10. Covering down
   The aim of this section is to prove the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7). Suppose that G is
a supercomplex and U is a вҖҳrandom-likeвҖҷ subset of V (G). The Cover down lemma shows the
existence of a вҖҳcleaning graphвҖҷ H вҲ— so that for any sparse leftover graph LвҲ— , G[H вҲ— вҲӘ LвҲ— ] has an
F -packing covering all edges of H вҲ— вҲӘ LвҲ— except possibly some inside U .
   We now briefly sketch how one can attempt to construct such a graph H вҲ— . As in Section 7.1,
for an edge e, we refer to |e вҲ© U | as its type. For the moment, suppose that H вҲ— and LвҲ— are given.
A natural way (for divisibility reasons) to try to cover all edges of H вҲ— вҲӘ LвҲ— which are not inside U
is to first cover all type-0-edges, then all type-1-edges, etc. and finally all type-(r вҲ’ 1)-edges. It
is comparatively easy to cover all type-0-edges. The reason for this is that a type-0-edge can be
covered by a copy of F that contains no other type-0-edge. Thus, if H вҲ— is a random subgraph of
G(r) вҲ’ G(r) [V (G) \ U ], then every type-0-edge (from LвҲ— ) is contained in many copies of F . Since
вҲҶ(LвҲ— ) is very small, this allows us to apply Corollary 6.9 in order to cover all type-0-edges with
edge-disjoint copies of F .
   The situation is very different for edges of higher types. Suppose that for some i вҲҲ [r вҲ’ 1], we
have already covered all edges of types 0, . . . , r вҲ’ i вҲ’ 1 and now want to cover all edges of type
r вҲ’ i. Every such edge contains a unique S вҲҲ V (G)\U        i    . As indicated in Section 7.1, we seek to
                                               V (G)\U 
cover all edges containing a fixed S вҲҲ             i     simultaneously using Proposition 7.9 as follows:
            V (F )                                        V (G)\U 
Let T вҲҲ        i    .  Roughly  speaking, for every  S  вҲҲ      i    , we reserve a random subgraph HS of
G(S)[U ](rвҲ’i) and protect all the HS вҖҷs when applying the nibble. Let L be the leftover resulting
from this application and let LS := L(S). Assuming that there are no more leftover edges of
types 0, . . . , r вҲ’ i вҲ’ 1 implies that LS вҠҶ G(S)[U ](rвҲ’i) and that HS вҲӘ LS is F (T )-divisible. We want
to use (вҲ—)rвҲ’i inductively to find a well separated F (T )-decomposition FS of HS вҲӘ LS (provided
that HS вҲӘ LS is quasirandom). Using Proposition 7.9, FS can then be вҖҳextendedвҖҷ to an F -packing
S вҠі FS which covers all edges that contain S. The hope is that the HS вҖҷs do not intersect too
much, so that it is possible to find an F (T )-decomposition FS for each S such that the extended
62                              S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



F -packings S вҠі FS are r-disjoint. Their union would then yield an F -packing covering all edges
of type r вҲ’ i.
   There are two natural candidates for selecting HS :
    (A) Choose HS by including every edge of G(S)[U ](rвҲ’i) with probability ОҪ.
    (B) Choose a random subset US of U of size ПҒ|U | and let HS := G(S)(rвҲ’i) [US ].
The advantage of Strategy (A) is that HS вҲӘ LS is quasirandom if LS is sparse. This is not
the case for (B): even if the maximum degree of LS is sublinear, its edges might be spread out
over the whole of U (while HS is restricted to US ). Unfortunately, when pursuing Strategy (A),
the HS intersect too much, so it is not clear how to find the desired decompositions due to the
interference between different HS . However, it turns out that under the additional assumption
that V (LS ) вҠҶ US , Strategy (B) does work. We call the corresponding result the вҖҳLocalised cover
down lemmaвҖҷ (Lemma 10.8).
   We will combine both strategies as follows: For each S, we will choose HS as in (A) and US as
in (B) and let JS := G(S)(rвҲ’i) [US ]. In a first step we use HS to find an F (T )-packing covering
all edges e вҲҲ HS вҲӘ LS with e 6вҠҶ US , and then afterwards we apply the Localised cover down
lemma to cover all remaining edges. Note that the first step resembles the original problem: We
are given a graph HS вҲӘ LS on U and want to cover all edges that are not inside US вҠҶ U . But
the resulting types are now more restricted. This enables us to prove a more general Cover down
lemma, the вҖҳCover down lemma for setupsвҖҷ (Lemma 10.24), by induction on r вҲ’ i, which will allow
us to perform the first step in the above combined strategy for all S simultaneously.

10.1. Systems and focuses. In this subsection, we prove the Localised cover down lemma,
which shows that Strategy (B) works under the assumption that each LS is вҖҳlocalisedвҖҷ.
Definition 10.1. Given i вҲҲ N0 , an i-system in a set V is a collection S of distinct subsets of
V of size i. A subset of V is called S-important if it contains some S вҲҲ S, otherwise we call it
S-unimportant. We say that U = (US )SвҲҲS is a focus for S if for each S вҲҲ S, US is a subset of
V \ S.
Definition 10.2. Let G be a complex and S an i-system in V (G). We call G r-exclusive with
respect to S if every e вҲҲ G with |e| вүҘ r contains at most one element of S. Let U be a focus for
S. If G is r-exclusive with respect to S, the following functions are well-defined: For r вҖІ вүҘ r, let
ErвҖІ denote the set of S-important r вҖІ -sets in G. Define П„rвҖІ : ErвҖІ вҶ’ [r вҖІ вҲ’ i]0 as П„rвҖІ (e) := |e вҲ© US |,
                                                                                     вҖІ
where S is the unique S вҲҲ S contained in e. We call П„rвҖІ the type function of G(r ) , S, U .

10.2. Partition pairs. We now develop the appropriate framework to be able to state the Cover
down lemma for setups (Lemma 10.24). Recall that we will consider (and cover) r-sets separately
according to their type. The type of an r-set e naturally imposes constraints on the type of an
f -set which covers e. We will need to track and adjust the densities of r-sets with respect to
f -sets for each pair of types separately. This gives rise to the following concepts of partition pairs
and partition regularity (see Section 10.3). We will sometimes refer to r-sets as вҖҳedgesвҖҷ and to
f -sets as вҖҳcliquesвҖҷ.
   Let X be a set. We say that P = (X1 , . . . , Xa ) is an ordered partition of X if the Xi are
disjoint subsets of X whose union is X. We let P(i) := Xi and P([i]) := (X1 , . . . , Xi ). If
P = (X1 , . . . , Xa ) is an ordered partition of X and X вҖІ вҠҶ X, we let P[X вҖІ ] denote the ordered
partition (X1 вҲ© X вҖІ , . . . , Xa вҲ© X вҖІ ) of X вҖІ . If {X вҖІ , X вҖІвҖІ } is a partition of X, P вҖІ = (X1вҖІ , . . . , XaвҖІ ) is an
ordered partition of X вҖІ and P вҖІвҖІ = (X1вҖІвҖІ , . . . , XbвҖІвҖІ ) is an ordered partition of X вҖІвҖІ , we let
                                    P вҖІ вҠ” P вҖІвҖІ := (X1вҖІ , . . . , XaвҖІ , X1вҖІвҖІ , . . . , XbвҖІвҖІ ).
Definition 10.10. Let G be a complex and let f > r вүҘ 1. An (r, f )-partition pair of G is a pair
(Pr , Pf ), where Pr is an ordered partition of G(r) and Pf is an ordered partition of G(f ) , such
that for all E вҲҲ Pr and Q вҲҲ Pf , every Q вҲҲ Q contains the same number C(E, Q) of elements
from E. We call C : Pr Г— Pf вҶ’ [ fr ]0 the containment function of the partition pair. We say that
                                    

(Pr , Pf ) is upper-triangular if C(Pr (в„“), Pf (k)) = 0 whenever в„“ > k.

   Clearly, for every Q вҲҲ Pf , EвҲҲPr C(E, Q) = fr . If (Pr , Pf ) is an (r, f )-partition pair of G
                                  P                     

and GвҖІ вҠҶ G is a subcomplex, we define
                                     (Pr , Pf )[GвҖІ ] := (Pr [GвҖІ(r) ], Pf [GвҖІ(f ) ]).
Clearly, (Pr , Pf )[GвҖІ ] is an (r, f )-partition pair of GвҖІ .
Example 10.11. Suppose that G is a complex and U вҠҶ V (G). For в„“ вҲҲ [r]0 , define Eв„“ :=
{e вҲҲ G(r) : |e вҲ© U | = в„“}. For k вҲҲ [f ]0 , define Qk := {Q вҲҲ G(f ) : |Q вҲ© U | = k}. Let
Pr := (E0 , . . . , Er ) and Pf := (Q0 , . . . , Qf ). Then clearly (Pr , Pf ) is an (r, f )-partition pair of G,
where the containment function is given by C(Eв„“ , Qk ) = kв„“ frвҲ’в„“
                                                                       вҲ’k
                                                                                . In particular, C(Eв„“ , Qk ) = 0
whenever в„“ > k or k > f вҲ’ r + в„“. We say that (Pr , Pf ) is the (r, f )-partition pair of G, U .
   The partition pairs we use are generalisations of the above example. More precisely, suppose
that G is a complex, S is an i-system in V (G) and U is a focus for S. Moreover, assume that G

every Q вҲҲ Qk contains exactly kв„“ frвҲ’iвҲ’в„“

S-unimportant edges and cliques. It turns out that it is useful to assume that the unimportant

  The next proposition summarises basic properties of an (r, f )-partition pair of G, S, U .
Proposition 10.12. Let 0 вүӨ i < r < f and suppose that G is a complex, S is an i-system in
V (G) and U is a focus for S. Moreover, assume that G is r-exclusive with respect to S. Let
(Pr , Pf ) be an (r, f )-partition pair of G, S, U with containment function C. Then the following
hold:
 (P1вҖІ ) |Pr | = r + 1 and |Pf | = f + 1;

70                                S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



 (P3вҖІ ) (Pr , Pf ) is upper-triangular;
 (P4вҖІ ) C(Pr (в„“), Pf (k)) = 0 whenever both в„“ > i and k > f вҲ’ r + в„“;

 (P6вҖІ ) if i = 0, S = {вҲ…} and U = {U } for some U вҠҶ V (G), then the (unique) (r, f )-partition
        pair of G, S, U is the (r, f )-partition pair of G, U (cf. Example 10.11);
 (P7вҖІ ) for every subcomplex GвҖІ вҠҶ G, (Pr , Pf )[GвҖІ ] is an (r, f )-partition pair of GвҖІ , S, U .
Proof. Clearly, (P1вҖІ ), (P2вҖІ ) and (P6вҖІ ) hold, and it is also straightforward to check (P7вҖІ ).
Moreover, (P3вҖІ ) holds because of (P3) and (10.6). The latter also implies (P4вҖІ ).
  Finally, consider (P5вҖІ ). For в„“ вҲҲ [i], this holds since (Pr ([i]), Pf ([i])) is admissible, so assume
that в„“ > i. We have Pr (в„“) = П„rвҲ’1 (в„“ вҲ’ i вҲ’ 1). Let S вҲҲ S, h вҲҲ [r вҲ’ i]0 and B вҠҶ G(S)(h) with

10.3. Partition regularity.
Definition 10.13. Let G be a complex on n vertices and (Pr , Pf ) an (r, f )-partition pair of G

(10.7)                                 |(Pf (k))(e)| = (aв„“,k Вұ Оө)nf вҲ’r ,
where we view Pf (k) as a subgraph of G(f ) . If E вҠҶ Pr (в„“) and Q вҠҶ Pf (k), we will often write
A(E, Q) instead of aв„“,k .
     For A вҲҲ [0, 1]aГ—b with 1 вүӨ t вүӨ a вүӨ b, we define
       вҖў min\ (A) := min{aj,j : j вҲҲ [a]} as the minimum value on the diagonal,
       вҖў min\t (A) := min{aj,j+bвҲ’a : j вҲҲ {a вҲ’ t + 1, . . . , a}} and
       вҖў min\\t (A) := min{min\ (A), min\t (A)}.
Note that min\\rвҲ’i+1 (A) is the minimum value of the entries in A that correspond to the entries
marked with вҲ— in Figure 1.

   In the proof of the Cover down lemma for setups, we face (amongst others) the following
two challenges: (i) given an (Оө, A, f, r)-regular complex G for some suitable A, we need to find
an efficient F -packing in G; (ii) if A is not suitable for (i), we need to find a вҖҳrepresentativeвҖҷ
subcomplex GвҖІ of G which is (Оө, AвҖІ , f, r)-regular for some AвҖІ that is suitable for (i). The strategy
to implement (i) is similar to that of the Boost lemma (Lemma 6.3): We randomly sparsify G(f )
according to a suitably chosen (non-uniform) probability distribution in order to find Y вҲ— вҠҶ G(f )
such that G[Y вҲ— ] is (Оө, d, f, r)-regular. We can then apply the Boosted nibble lemma (Lemma 6.4).
The desired probability distribution arises from a non-negative solution to the equation Ax = 1.
The following condition on A allows us to find such a solution (cf. Proposition 10.16).
Definition 10.15. We say that A вҲҲ [0, 1]aГ—b is diagonal-dominant if aв„“,k вүӨ ak,k /2(a вҲ’ в„“) for all
1 вүӨ в„“ < k вүӨ min{a, b}.
   Definition 10.15 also allows us to achieve (ii). Given some A, we can find a вҖҳrepresentat-
iveвҖҷ subcomplex GвҖІ of G which is (Оө, AвҖІ , f, r)-regular for some AвҖІ that is diagonal-dominant (cf.
Lemma 10.20).
Proposition 10.16. Let A вҲҲ [0, 1]aГ—b be upper-triangular and diagonal-dominant with a вүӨ b.
Then there exists x вҲҲ [0, 1]b such that x вүҘ min\ (A)/4b and Ax = min\ (A)1.

   The following concept of a setup turns out to be the appropriate generalisation of Definition 7.1
to i-systems and partition pairs.
Definition 10.18 (Setup). Let G be a complex on n vertices and 0 вүӨ i < r < f . We say that
S, U , (Pr , Pf ) form an (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r, i)-setup for G if there exists an f -graph Y on V (G) such that
the following hold:
   (S1) S is an i-system in V (G) such that G is r-exclusive with respect to S; U is a Вө-focus for
         S and (Pr , Pf ) is an (r, f )-partition pair of G, S, U ;
   (S2) there exists a matrix A вҲҲ [0, 1](r+1)Г—(f +1) with min\\rвҲ’i+1 (A) вүҘ Оҫ such that G[Y ] is
         (Оө, A, f, r)-regular with respect to (Pr , Pf )[G[Y ]] = (Pr , Pf [Y ]);
   (S3) every S-unimportant e вҲҲ G(r) is contained in at least Оҫ(Вөn)f S-unimportant Q вҲҲ G[Y ](f +r) ,
         and for every S-important e вҲҲ G(r) with e вҠҮ S вҲҲ S, we have |G[Y ](f +r) (e)[US ]| вүҘ Оҫ(Вөn)f ;
   (S4) Tfor all S вҲҲ S, h вҲҲ [r вҲ’ i]0 and all B вҠҶ G(S)(h) with 1 вүӨ |B| вүӨ 2h we have that
             bвҲҲB G(S вҲӘ b)[US ] is an (Оө, Оҫ, f вҲ’ i вҲ’ h, r вҲ’ i вҲ’ h)-complex.
Moreover, if (S1)вҖ“(S4) are true and A is diagonal-dominant, then we say that S, U , (Pr , Pf ) form
a diagonal-dominant (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r, i)-setup for G.
  Note that (S4) implies that G(S)[US ] is an (Оө, Оҫ, f вҲ’ i, r вҲ’ i)-supercomplex for every S вҲҲ S,
but is stronger in the sense that B is not restricted to US . The following observation shows that
Definition 10.18 does indeed generalise Definition 7.1. (Recall that the partition pair of G, U was
defined in Example 10.11.) We will use it to derive the Cover down lemma from the more general
Cover down lemma for setups.
Proposition 10.19. Let G be a complex on n vertices and suppose that U вҠҶ V (G) is (Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r)-
random in G. Let (Pr , Pf ) be the (r, f )-partition pair of G, U . Then {вҲ…}, {U }, (Pr , Pf ) form an
(Оө, Вө, ВөМғОҫ, f, r, 0)-setup for G, where ВөМғ := (min {Вө, 1 вҲ’ Вө})f вҲ’r .
Proof. We first check (S1). Clearly, S is a 0-system in V (G). Moreover, G is trivially r-exclusive
with respect to S since |S| < 2. Moreover, by (R1), U is a Вө-focus for S, and (Pr , Pf ) is an
(r, f )-partition pair of G, S, U by (P6вҖІ ) in Proposition 10.12. Note that (S4) follows immediately
from (R4). In order to check (S2) and (S3), assume that Y вҠҶ G(f ) and d вүҘ Оҫ are such that (R2)
and (R3) hold. Clearly, all e вҲҲ G(r) are S-important, and by (R3), we have for all e вҲҲ G(r)
that |G[Y ](f +r) (e)[U ]| вүҘ Оҫ(Вөn)f , so (S3) holds. Finally, we have seen in Example 10.14 that there
exists a matrix A вҲҲ [0, 1](r+1)Г—(f +1) with min\\rвҲ’i+1 (A) вүҘ ВөМғОҫ such that G[Y ] is (Оө, A, f, r)-regular
with respect to (Pr , Pf [Y ]).                                                                       

   The final tool that we need is the following lemma. Given a setup in a supercomplex G and

10.4. Proof of the Cover down lemma. In this subsection, we state and prove the Cover
down lemma for setups and deduce the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7).

Definition 10.23. Let F and G be r-graphs, let S be an i-system in V (G), and let U be a focus
for S. We say that G is F -divisible with respect to S, U , if for all S вҲҲ S and all T вҠҶ V (G) \ S
with |T | вүӨ r вҲ’ i вҲ’ 1 and |T \ US | вүҘ 1, we have Deg(F )i+|T | | |G(S вҲӘ T )|.

   Note that if G is F -divisible, then it is F -divisible with respect to any i-system and any
associated focus.
   Recall that a setup for G was defined in Definition 10.18, and G being (Оҫ, f, r)-dense with
respect to H вҠҶ G(r) in Definition 7.6. We will prove the Cover down lemma for setups by
induction on r вҲ’ i. We will deduce the Cover down lemma by applying this lemma with i = 0.

Lemma 10.24 (Cover down lemma for setups). Let 1/n вүӘ 1/Оә вүӘ Оі вүӘ Оө вүӘ ОҪ вүӘ Вө, Оҫ, 1/f and
0 вүӨ i < r < f . Let F be a weakly regular r-graph on f vertices. Assume that (вҲ—)в„“ is true for
all в„“ вҲҲ [r вҲ’ i вҲ’ 1]. Let G be a complex on n vertices and suppose that S, U , (Pr , Pf ) form an
                                                                                    вҖІ
(Оө, Вө, Оҫ, f, r, i)-setup for G. For r вҖІ вүҘ r, let П„rвҖІ denote the type function of G(r ) , S, U . Then the
following hold.
      (i) Let GМғ be a complex on V (G) with G вҠҶ GМғ such that GМғ is (Оө, f, r)-dense with respect to
          G(r) вҲ’ П„rвҲ’1 (0). Then there exists a subgraph H вҲ— вҠҶ G(r) вҲ’ П„rвҲ’1 (0) with вҲҶ(H вҲ— ) вүӨ ОҪn such
          that for any LвҲ— вҠҶ GМғ(r) with вҲҶ(LвҲ— ) вүӨ Оіn and H вҲ— вҲӘ LвҲ— being F -divisible with respect to
          S, U and any (r + 1)-graph O вҲ— on V (G) with вҲҶ(O вҲ— ) вүӨ Оіn, there exists a Оә-well separated
          F -packing in GМғ[H вҲ— вҲӘ LвҲ— ] вҲ’ OвҲ— which covers all edges of LвҲ— , and all S-important edges of

     (ii) If G(r) is F -divisible with respect to S, U and the setup is diagonal-dominant, then there
          exists a 2Оә-well separated F -packing in G which covers all S-important r-edges except

  Before proving Lemma 10.24, we show how it implies the Cover down lemma (Lemma 7.7).

proof of Lemma 10.24 itself.

                                        11. Achieving divisibility
    It remains to show that we can turn every F -divisible r-graph G into an F вҲ— -divisible r-graph
GвҖІ by removing a sparse F -decomposable subgraph of G, that is, to prove Lemma 9.4. Note that
in Lemma 9.4, we do not need to assume that F вҲ— is weakly regular. On the other hand, our
argument heavily relies on the assumption that F вҲ— is F -decomposable.
    We first sketch the argument. Let F вҲ— be F -decomposable, let bk := Deg(F вҲ— )k and hk :=
Deg(F )k . Clearly, we have hk | bk . First, consider the case k = 0. Then b0 = |F вҲ— | and h0 = |F |.
We know that |G| is divisible by h0 . Let 0 вүӨ x < b0 be such that |G| вүЎ x mod b0 . Since h0
divides |G| and b0 , it follows that x = ah0 for some 0 вүӨ a < b0 /h0 . Thus, removing a edge-disjoint
copies of F from G yields an r-graph GвҖІ such that |GвҖІ | = |G| вҲ’ ah0 вүЎ 0 mod b0 , as desired. This
will in fact be the first step of our argument.
    We then proceed by achieving Deg(GвҖІ )1 вүЎ 0 mod b1 . Suppose that the vertices of GвҖІ are
ordered v1 , . . . , vn . We will construct a degree shifter which will fix the degree of v1 by allowing
the degree of v2 to change, whereas all other degrees are unaffected (modulo b1 ). Step by step, we
will fix all the degrees from v1 , . . . , vnвҲ’1 . Fortunately, the degree of vn will then automatically be
divisible by b1 . For k > 1, we will proceed similarly, but the procedure becomes more intricate. It
is in general impossible to shift degree from one k-set to another one without affecting the degrees
84                                     S. GLOCK, D. KUМҲHN, A. LO AND D. OSTHUS



of any other k-set. Roughly speaking, the degree shifter will contain a set of 2k special вҖҳroot verti-
cesвҖҷ, and the degrees of precisely 2k k-subsets of this root set change, whereas all other k-degrees
are unaffected (modulo bk ). This will allow us to fix all the degrees of k-sets in GвҖІ except the ones
inside some final (2k вҲ’ 1)-set, where we use induction on k as well. Fortunately, the remaining
k-sets will again automatically satisfy the desired divisibility condition (cf. Lemma 11.5).
   The proof of Lemma 9.4 divides into three parts. In the first subsection, we will construct the
degree shifters. In the second subsection, we show on a very abstract level (without considering
a particular host graph) how the shifting has to proceed in order to achieve overall divisibility.
Finally, we will prove Lemma 9.4 by embedding our constructed shifters (using Lemma 5.20)
according to the given shifting procedure.

11.1. Degree shifters. The aim of this subsection is to show the existence of certain r-graphs
which we call degree shifters. They allow us to locally вҖҳshiftвҖҷ degree among the k-sets of some
host graph G.

11.2. Shifting procedure. In the previous section, we constructed degree shifters which allow
us to locally change the degrees of k-sets in some host graph. We will now show how to combine
these local shifts in order to transform any given F -divisible r-graph G into an F вҲ— -divisible r-
graph. It turns out to be more convenient to consider the shifting for вҖҳr-set functionsвҖҷ rather
than r-graphs. We will then recover the graph theoretical statement by considering a graph as
an indicator set function (see below).
   Let ПҶ : Vr вҶ’ Z. (Think of ПҶ as the multiplicity function of a multi-r-graph.) We extend ПҶ to

Clearly, if G and GвҖІ are edge-disjoint, then we have 1G + 1GвҖІ = 1GвҲӘGвҖІ . Moreover, for an r-graph
F , G is F -divisible if and only if 1G is (Deg(F )0 , . . . , Deg(F )rвҲ’1 )-divisible.
   As mentioned before, our strategy is to successively fix the degrees of k-sets until we have fixed
the degrees of all k-sets except possibly the degrees of those k-sets contained in some final vertex
set K which is too small as to continue with the shifting. However, as the following lemma shows,
divisibility is then automatically satisfied for all the k-sets lying inside K. For this to work it is
essential that the degrees of all i-sets for i < k are already fixed.

  We now define a more abstract version of degree shifters, which we call adapters. They represent
the effect of shifters and will finally be replaced by shifters again.
Definition 11.6 (x-adapter). Let V be a vertex set and k, r, b0 , . . . , bk , hk вҲҲ N be such that
k < r and hk | bk . For distinct vertices x01 , . . . , x0k , x11 , . . . , x1k in V , we say that П„ : Vr вҶ’ Z is an
(x01 , . . . , x0k , x11 , . . . , x1k )-adapter with respect to (b0 , . . . , bk ; hk ) if П„ is (b0 , . . . , bkвҲ’1 )-divisible and
for all S вҲҲ Vk ,
                        
                                             (     P
                                              (вҲ’1) iвҲҲ[k] zi hk mod bk if S = {xzi i : i вҲҲ [k]},
                                   П„ (S) вүЎ
                                              0 mod bk                         otherwise.
   Note that such an adapter П„ is (b0 , . . . , bkвҲ’1 , hk )-divisible.
Fact 11.7. If T is an x-shifter with respect to F, F вҲ— , then 1T is an x-adapter with respect to
(Deg(F вҲ— )0 , . . . , Deg(F вҲ— )k ; Deg(F )k ).
   The following definition is crucial for the shifting procedure. Given some function ПҶ, we intend
to add adapters in order to obtain a divisible function. Every adapter is characterised by a tuple
x consisting of 2k distinct vertices, which tells us where to apply the adapter. All these tuples
are contained within a multiset в„Ұ, which we call a balancer. в„Ұ is capable of dealing with any
input function ПҶ in the sense that there is a multisubset of в„Ұ which tells us where to apply the
adapters in order to make ПҶ divisible. Moreover, as we finally want to replace the adapters by
shifters (and thus embed them into some host graph), there must not be too many of them.
Definition 11.8 (balancer). Let r, k, b0 , . . . , bk вҲҲ N with k < r and let U, V be sets with U вҠҶ V .
Let в„Ұk be a multiset containing ordered tuples x = (x1 , . . . , x2k ), where x1 , . . . , x2k вҲҲ U are
distinct. We say that в„Ұk is a (b0 , . . . , bk )-balancer for V with uniformity r acting on U if for
any hk вҲҲ N with hk | bk , the following holds: let ПҶ : Vr вҶ’ Z be any (b0 , . . . , bkвҲ’1 , hk )-divisible
function such that S вҠҶ U whenever S вҲҲ Vk and ПҶ(S) 6вүЎ 0 mod
                                                     
                                                                        P bk . There exists a multisubset

with respect to (b0 , . . . , bk ; hk ).

shifters in a suitable way, which is achieved via Lemma 5.20. The following fact will help us to
verify the conditions of Lemma 11.9.

                                       12. Recent developments
   Since the initial submission of the current manuscript, there has been the following closely
related work: firstly, for a short expository paper which demonstrates the iterative absorption
method with the example of triangle decompositions, see [5].
   The main result of this paper (the existence of F -decompositions of divisible typical hyper-
graphs) has been used recently by Glock, Joos, KuМҲhn and Osthus [18] to settle a long-standing
conjecture of Chung, Diaconis and Graham on the existence of universal cycles.
   Amongst others, Keevash [25] proved results on the existence of resolvable designs, of designs
in a partite setting as well as F -designs.

   We are grateful to Ben Barber, John Lapinskas and Richard Montgomery for helpful discus-
sions.
